(The information about it can be read on Julie Kagawa's blog) <br/><br/>As said in her blog post, there are many reasons why they chose to "remake" the cover of <i>The Immortal Rules</i> series. Some of these reasons include the original cover not being "dystopian enough". <br/><br/>Ahem. <br/><br/>Sorry. I just choked. Seriously. I did not just do that because I think its BS. Nope. Not at all. <br/><br/>What in the <i>world</i> mak</span>
  <span id="freeText5294632203816107488" style="display:none">Okay. Was I the only one who thought that this blue cover was just a placeholder? <br><br>Well its not. Its the <i>actual cover</i>. (The information about it can be read on Julie Kagawa's blog) <br><br>As said in her blog post, there are many reasons why they chose to "remake" the cover of <i>The Immortal Rules</i> series. Some of these reasons include the original cover not being "dystopian enough". <br><br>Ahem. <br><br>Sorry. I just choked. Seriously. I did not just do that because I think its BS. Nope. Not at all. <br><br>What in the <i>world</i> makes a cover look "dystopian"? Hunger Games cover = pin. Divergent cover = ball of fire. Delirium = girl. Is there a certain "dystopian" theme going on here? I'm not going to look at a cover and say "Oh yeah, that's totally dystopian. I can tell from the spindly tree." READ THE DESCRIPTION, DAMMIT. <br><br><br>Although...I do have to agree with the fact that Alyson didn't look - wait for it - <i>asian</i> enough on the cover of the first book. Yes. That is one of the reasons why they're changing it. Although, I don't think you can really judge the cover model that much - Alysson was never directly stated to be of asian decent. The only clue we have is someone calling her "squinty-eyes", but even then its pretty clear from the author's notes that she is (if you get my drift). But its not like things like this haven't been done before - I mean, look at some of those book covers out there. Some of them are completely whacked. Either way, the cover doesn't really have to influence how we imagine the characters - as long as the author does a good job explaining them, we can throw away the cover flap and come up with our own images. <br><br>So. Is this cover going to make <i>The Immortal Rules</i> more popular? My opinion? I think not. They're not flashy. They're not eye-catching at all. The original cover of the first book? Completely noticeable. Its <i>creepy</i>. People like creepy. However, I had to remove the cover sleeve when I was reading it, because people would stare at me funny when they saw a <i>bleeding eyeball</i> on the front of the book, so I'm not really one to judge. These new covers? They won't entrance people like the first ones. Its just so...normal. Nothing to really hint at what is behind the cover. <br><br>I don't know. Are these new covers a mistake? Its hard to tell. Although I can hint the subtle wanting to seem like every other harmless dystopian book. But when people read "vampires" they'll either run the other way, or get hooked - without a kick-ass cover, I'm guessing that people will be running. <br><br>***<br><br><a href="http://s1103.photobucket.com/albums/g475/TheSyxx66/Tumblr%20Gifs/?action=view&amp;current=KermitFreakingOut.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_565059141" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/565059141" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/565059141?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=quest">quest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=on-the-run">on-the-run</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer565059141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15426454804839046789">There are two types of families, one we are born to, and one we choose. We can't choose the former, the latter forms almost inadvertently sometimes, but they're just as important. My friend told me that once, and that quote leaped to my mind as I read this book. I love the twisted dynamics of the family that poor Allison has got herself into in <i>The Eternity Cure</i>. I didn't really like the concept of this series when I reluctantly started reading it, but <i>The Immortal Rules</i> turned out to be better </span>
  <span id="freeText15426454804839046789" style="display:none">There are two types of families, one we are born to, and one we choose. We can't choose the former, the latter forms almost inadvertently sometimes, but they're just as important. My friend told me that once, and that quote leaped to my mind as I read this book. I love the twisted dynamics of the family that poor Allison has got herself into in <i>The Eternity Cure</i>. I didn't really like the concept of this series when I reluctantly started reading it, but <i>The Immortal Rules</i> turned out to be better than anything I could have imagined, and I had been waiting with bated breath for the sequel. I was not the least bit disappointed; this has been more than worth the wait.<br /><br />Allison has left Zeke behind in her quest to find her creator, Kanin. It's not like Allie was ever truly helpless and innocent, growing up scrounging to survive and looking out mostly for herself, but she is harder in this book. She's learned through experience, she's tough, she's a survivor with the accompanied scars.<br /><br />Allie has been wandering around by herself for four months, following the gut instincts that tell her where her sire is being kept and tortured. She is more accepting of her vampire nature now, she takes blood when she needs to; she doesn't like it, but she is not completely mired in self-loathing when she does it. It's survival now.<br /><br />Against her will, Allie joins forces with her "brother," the twisted Jackal. Together, the two return to New Covington to try and free Kanin. They encounter some old characters, and are betrayed by someone Allie never thought she'd see again. I can't even mention his name, I am so incomprehensively angry at that stupid asshole, after everything Allison did for him...ok, deep breath. Not a real person. No need to lose my temper over a fictional character. Whew.<br /><br />The only flaw I found in this book was with Zeke. Ugh. Zeke actually plays a role in the previous one, and he should have stayed there in the good, but distant past where he belonged. His presence in this book, I felt, did more harm than good. He and Jackal spent more time at each other's throat than actually contributing anything to help find/free Kanin. I'm amazed that they got anything done with Zeke around. And yeah, getting a human inside New Covington...not the easiest thing to do.<br /><br />They should have left him in the fringe, especially when Zeke’s main contributing role in this book seem to be his ability to add more pages to the book in terms of whining and crying and creating conflict. Some characters are inserted solely for verbal flufferage. Zeke becomes one of them in this book. I wish he had been turned into a vampire in the first book. At least then he wouldn't be a waste of air.<br /><br />OK FINE I KNOW HE PLAYS A CRITICAL PART IN THE BOOK BUT I STILL DON'T LIKE HIM.<br /><br />I am impressed with Allie's behavior in this book. She's <i>rational</i>. She hates Jackal and his previous actions. She knows he is capable of horrible things, but she works with him anyway without being a screeching, whining, and contrary harpy. She does what she needs to in order to get shit done. That, my friend, is the type of heroine I can get behind. Together, she, Kanin, and Jackal are an odd family, but they work well together and they are connected through a similar goal. Dysfunctional though they are, I love how they work together...and yet they get along better than some families I know.<br /><br />Did I mention that Julie Kagawa is a kick-ass writer? The ability to create characters that arouse such strong emotions (not that of the "I'm severely annoyed by you" kind. Any writer can create an annoying character, sometimes an unwittingly annoying character. *cough*Luce*cough*Bella*cough*Calder*cough*) It takes true talent to create a character with...actual character, that with which we can sympathize and hate and grow angry.<br /><br />Jackal is by far the best character in this book. I think I like him even more than Allie here. He is a lot more authentic. He doesn't try to hide his true nature, or who he is. It's refreshing, especially when everyone is so lacking in confidence. He's certainly a better match for Allie. Blood siblings, not real siblings, right? Anyone with me? There's always book 3! Not really, but one can hope.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15426454804839046789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_324263174" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/324263174" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/324263174?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=they-are-so-awesome-hot-and-stuff">they-are-so-awesome-hot-and-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-couple">favorite-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=cut-my-heart-out">cut-my-heart-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=age-mature-young-adult">age-mature-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=made-me-smile-or-laugh">made-me-smile-or-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=they-are-so-cute-its-unbearable">they-are-so-cute-its-unbearable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroes-please">be-my-heroes-please</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer324263174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5796069864522228493"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376916ra/732058.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“There are no good choices, Allison,” Kanin offered in a quiet voice. “There are only those you can live with, and those you can work to change.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376916i/732059._SX540_.png' width='400' height='210' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>I need to recover from this one. </b>My mind is blown into pieces. My heart has been repeatedly smashed into the wall, picked up and smashed again. But thankfully <b>i am still alive.</b><br/><br/><b>This sequel is probably the best book i have read this year and in a while. </b>Absolutely amazing, full of action, fast paced and totally ended wit</span>
  <span id="freeText5796069864522228493" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376916ra/732058.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“There are no good choices, Allison,” Kanin offered in a quiet voice. “There are only those you can live with, and those you can work to change.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376916i/732059._SX540_.png" width="400" height="210" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I need to recover from this one. </b>My mind is blown into pieces. My heart has been repeatedly smashed into the wall, picked up and smashed again. But thankfully <b>i am still alive.</b><br><br><b>This sequel is probably the best book i have read this year and in a while. </b>Absolutely amazing, full of action, fast paced and totally ended with a <b>freaking cliffhanger</b> over which i am still being mad about. <br><br>And this <b>cliffhanger</b>... oh my god. She can't do this to her fans!!!!! it's unacceptable! I am not ashamed to admit that i cried over it. I just did and i couldn't help myself.<br><br>Anyway..... it was just <b>perfect</b>. Well, bluntly said, i am in love with this book and this author. And i am in love with her characters. But! One thing! Could the cover be any more worse than it is? The blue one looks like placeholder and the both girl ones are horrible. :( Well, you cant judge book by it's cover.<br><br>P.s.<b> i am totally Team Kanin</b> even though it's not love triangle T_T<br>first time i actually want a book to have it.<br><br><b>*this review contains <i>slight</i> spoilers for this book, nothing serious or worth killing me for, and <u> spoilers for first book </u>- proceed with caution.*</b><br>___________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>STORY</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>___________________________________________<br><br><br>After leaving Eden, Allie starts searching for her sire, Kanin, who was being tortured by a vicious vampire Sarren, out of revenge. Since blood calls to blood, she wants to rescue him at all costs but accidentally stumbles on a person she expected the least - Jackal - her enemy and her blood brother.<br><br>And they are set on finding Kanin.....for different reasons. And she has to trust him - even though she can't. <br><br>Meanwhile...strange things happen within a certain town...and it has to be stopped. At all costs. No matter how.<br><br>~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~<br><br>The story was certainly far better than the first one. SO many plot twists happened and some of them i really hated. But, it made this book totally unexpected and strong. <br><br>I wouldn't call this story about love. Love is so little present in this book, and its all focused on the story, but it was there and it was beautiful. It's a story of a bond, of family and revenge. <br><br>~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~<br><br><b>Now....onto the spoiler part:<br>safe only for those who finished the book:<br>CONTAINS ABSOLUTELY HEAVY SPOILERS. YOU HAVE BEEN WARNED.</b><br><br>&gt;&gt;&gt; <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Oh my god. All things that happened killed my mind. First, we find out that Sarren is absolutely psychotic and his methods are horrible. Then, we find out that Kanin is held in the old city Allison lived in, and even worse, that Sarren stole the virus which was a form of red lung which now terrorizes the city. And then Zeke appears and comes to the rescue *swoons*....Jackal is being awesome asshole and all...and they finally rescue my honey Kanin.<br><br>I gotta say, i love Kanin, i love how he accepted everything...Allie's relationship with Zeke, even though he warned her of staying out of contacting the humans, and i loved him for it. And i secretly worship him with Allie. He finally spills his guts about many many things as well. Makes me love him even more.<br><br>But then shit starts happening and Kanin gets poisoned by that bastard Salazar, and the worst thing of all was when Zeke got infected too. I thought he was going to die.<br><br>But nothing prepared me for what Sarren did to Zeke......oh my god...that scene...i cried so much. Julie can't do this to us... i hate it! T_T It was completely and totally devastating and horrible. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> &lt;&lt;&lt;<br><br><br>___________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>CHARACTERS</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>___________________________________________<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Allie</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376916i/732062._SX540_.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"“I know what it’s like to miss someone. To feel like you’re just… wandering around, lost. And how you wish they were there, if only for a moment, just to point you in the right direction.”"</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Allison is strong, awesome and just fantastic. I love her character, i love her witness and i love her cunning. She still struggles to not be the monster the others are...she tries to be strong and not to kill innocent people - so she choose the lesser of two evils, and now hunts criminals and thugs. The only thing which makes her keep humanity is Zeke...He is sort of her limiter, and he became even more...he became her consciousness, her awareness of right and wrong.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>" “The lesser of two evils was still evil.” "</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>She wants to find Kanin at all costs, he after all, saved her life and she wants to return the favor....especially after all the dreams she saw about him....All the pain and misery he suffers at the hands of Sarren.<br><br>Her love with Zeke progresses and i was so happy for it... they are absolutely cute as a couple and both of them are just adorable ♥<br><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Zeke</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>" “I don't believe in fate," he said carefully, "but... I do believe everything happens for a reason. That there is some plan, some meaning to this darkness we live in.” "</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Yes. Zeke is back. Yes. If i could hug him, i would. He is just huggable person. Pure, honest and amazing (even when he keeps his secrets). And horribly optimistic. That part of him never changed...but some others did.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>" “Only death will take me away from you, vampire girl," he whispered. "And even then, I'll watch over you from wherever I end up.” "</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br> He truly accepted Allie for what she was, and he wants a chance with her, he doesn't see her as a monster she is, but as someone else...different vampire than he was used to hear about and see. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>" “You're still beautiful and dangerous and incredible, and I'll keep telling you that for as long as it takes you to believe it. But right now, all I want to do is kiss you, except I'm terrified that if I try you might throw me off this balcony.” "</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>But...he is bent on revenge and he wants to kill Jackal for all he had done to his family. And he won't back down easily...<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Kanin</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"“Because we must.” Kanin’s voice and expression remained the same. “Because there is nothing else we can do. Because there is no one else.” His voice dropped, becoming nearly inaudible. “I will put my trust in hope once more, and perhaps this time, it will be enough.”"</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Oh Kanin. This book is mostly oriented on his rescue....And the poor vamp has been suffering for so long. I love how he got through a transformation after the rescue. He was no longer a teacher, but he became a friend, a family. He is wonderful character, and i forgave him for everything and i wish other vampires and humans would too. He did whatever he could to save everyone and when the plan backfired, he got blamed for it. And now he has an army of pissed vamps and humans, and worst of all, Sarren, on his back. The worst thing of all is that he is so filled with regret, that it made him so much different. He doesn't want any more blood on his hands and he is forced to bear with it for the rest of his life...and we are talking about eternity.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “You will always be a monster - there is no turning back from it. But what kind of monster you become is entirely up to you.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Jackal</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Another snicker. “What you have to ask yourself,” he continued, “is whether I’m the type who would stay awake long enough to kill you after you fall asleep, or if I’m an early riser who would kill you before you woke up.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Oh Jackal...Jackal...Jackal...<br>He is the character who appears literally at the beginning of the book. I must say that i really did not like the bastard in the first book, being psychotic vampire who killed a lot of humans including Zeke's group,he just... grew on me. He is extremely sarcastic, and i mean it, his every sentence is sarcastic - and it made me laugh so many times. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>" “We’re both still here.”<br>He drew in a slow breath. “Allie…”<br>“Oh, don’t mind me,” came an extremely sarcastic voice near the wall. “You two go ahead and make out—I’ll just sit here and bleed quietly.” "</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>He hates it how Allison doesn't accept that she is vampire. He thinks that humans are meant to be ruled and therefore his controlling behaviour. But...he is quite complex and he is neither good nor bad...he is too complicated to understand if he is really good or if he is just plain bad. And when you read the book - you will know.<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Sarren</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Perhaps a song is worth a thousand<br>pictures, hmm?"</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Extremely psychotic vampire........and absolutely creepy...He is a picture of pure madness and disaster. Being totally crazy, he torments everyone he could get his hands on and he is professional at doing it. *shivers*<br><br>He takes a great pleasure at torture, and i just couldn't bear all he did to my lovely Kanin....<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Everyone else</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br><br>There are many, many characters which appear, and talking about them would be spoilerous, so i will refrain myself. But, i must say how disappointed i was by certain character...<br>___________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>OVERALL</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>___________________________________________<br><br>Wowowowoowowwowowowow. This series is one of those i love the most. Everything is done nicely, writing is amazing, it's a type of the book where you can easily imagine whole scenes and events. To me, it felt like watching a movie, and it is a rereading material kind of book. Everything was perfect, well done and fantastic. <br><br><b>If you haven't read these books, what are you waiting for - read them now!</b><br><br>But that cliffhanger is killing meeeeeeeeeeeeeeeee!<br>I can't wait for the final book (or at least i hope it will be)! <br><br><b>
  <i>This review can be found on my blog: <a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">infinity-of-time.blogspot.com</a> also known as... </i>
</b><br><a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/2013/05/the-eternity-cure-blood-of-eden-2-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363317i/714576.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br>____________________________________________ <br><br><b> MY BLOOD OF EDEN REVIEWS: </b><br><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/428203580" rel="nofollow noopener"> 'Til the World Ends (Blood of Eden, #0.5) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/324263158" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Immortal Rules (Blood of Eden, #1) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/324263174" <div id="review_3281757227" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3281757227" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40997852-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605132719p2/40997852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3281757227?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/40997852-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3281757227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15532707516654936150">I reached a point where I started believing that I outgrew YA. Repetitive plot and annoying characters –among other things- kept me away from this genre. I’m glad I decided to read this trilogy it’s quite refreshing. If I was true to myself –especially since it’s by no means a perfect book- I would’ve rated it 4 stars but honestly? This was too damn fun. <br/><br/>I read 92% of the book in one sitting before I went to sleep at 4 am yesterday. I could not stop reading. At that point, everything seemed to b</span>
  <span id="freeText15532707516654936150" style="display:none">I reached a point where I started believing that I outgrew YA. Repetitive plot and annoying characters –among other things- kept me away from this genre. I’m glad I decided to read this trilogy it’s quite refreshing. If I was true to myself –especially since it’s by no means a perfect book- I would’ve rated it 4 stars but honestly? This was too damn fun. <br /><br />I read 92% of the book in one sitting before I went to sleep at 4 am yesterday. I could not stop reading. At that point, everything seemed to be going in a direction, you know “the resolution”, so I figured I can finish it today as I had to wake up early. I finished the book during the car drive with my friends this morning and I WAS STUNNED. My eyes watered. I was NOT expecting that! How can everyone continue living as if nothing has happened after that ending? Kagawa is certainly not afraid to pull off merciless plot twists!<br /><br />So what did I love about this book?<br />✎	<b>Zeke.</b> He only did not feel important to me at all in book 1. Nor that interesting. But now? I adore him. He’s so sweet and different from the usual love interests, especially since Allie is in the power position here being the vampire. It was interesting to see it reversed!<br />✎	<b>The pace.</b> I honestly couldn’t put my kindle down. It was a very quick read and did not bore me once. It certainly doesn’t suffer from the second book syndrome. It doesn’t wait to start all the action.<br />✎	<b>Jackal.</b> Okay, we all agree that he’s fantastic. His witty remarks are fun and I enjoyed his banter with Allie. <br />✎	It was also interesting to see how Allie’s relationship with the guys developed. <br /><br />Sadly, I cannot but mention the weaknesses since they did annoy me.<br />✎	 I did not like Stick’s plot at all, especially at first. He’s just so pathetic.<br />✎	Some things are never explained (also I’m glad one of the questions in the first book were answered and stronger vampires can actually wake up once they sleep) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[like why did Zeke go to New Covington? Other than the fact it was his only lead to Allie –he knows it’s where she grew up- nothing hints she will be heading there. Also, how does he know the tunnels so well? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />That’s all I remember for now but I honestly highly recommend this trilogy if you’re looking for a fun YA to read. The new releases are mostly junk, I should dig more in the older ones because this book reminded me why this genre can be so entertaining!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15532707516654936150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10455174976215250540">The middle book in the trilogy and as with the first book I almost loved it, but not quite. My main issue was probably the sheer relentlessness of the action. I enjoy action and I enjoy a fast pace to a story, but there needs to be some peace occasionally and time to breathe and recover. I suppose the banter between Allie and Jackal is intended to bring some comic relief but it is only minor and not always especially funny. Nevertheless it is a good story and well told even if I did skim the fig</span>
  <span id="freeText10455174976215250540" style="display:none">The middle book in the trilogy and as with the first book I almost loved it, but not quite. My main issue was probably the sheer relentlessness of the action. I enjoy action and I enjoy a fast pace to a story, but there needs to be some peace occasionally and time to breathe and recover. I suppose the banter between Allie and Jackal is intended to bring some comic relief but it is only minor and not always especially funny. Nevertheless it is a good story and well told even if I did skim the fighting occasionally. Jackal is a great character and sometimes he is very funny. The ending is dramatic and a total cliff hanger so reading the third book is a requirement:)</span>

<div id="review_318438847" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/318438847" />
    <a title="Lucille" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2364631-lucille"><img alt="Lucille" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440217841p2/2364631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/318438847?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucille" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucille" href="/user/show/2364631-lucille">Lucille</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2364631-lucille?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2364631-lucille?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2364631-lucille?shelf=books-that-destroyed-me">books-that-destroyed-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer318438847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4927959129793144466"><b>AFTER RE-READING</b> <i>31 July 2013</i> I finally came up with my Top <s>10</s> 12 quotations. There are so many that I had a hard time narrowing it down to <s>ten</s> twelve.<br/><br/><b>1.</b> You and me, sister, we're exactly the same. Fight it as long as you want--in the end, the monster always wins. -Jackal<br/><br/><b>2.</b> You can't save anyone now. The requiem has started, and when the last melody plays, the only applause will be sweet, eternal silence. -Sarren<br/><br/><b>3.</b> In that moment, I'd never wanted to be human more, just so I could be with Ezekie</span>
  <span id="freeText4927959129793144466" style="display:none"><b>AFTER RE-READING</b> <i>31 July 2013</i> I finally came up with my Top <s>10</s> 12 quotations. There are so many that I had a hard time narrowing it down to <s>ten</s> twelve.<br><br><b>1.</b> You and me, sister, we're exactly the same. Fight it as long as you want--in the end, the monster always wins. -Jackal<br><br><b>2.</b> You can't save anyone now. The requiem has started, and when the last melody plays, the only applause will be sweet, eternal silence. -Sarren<br><br><b>3.</b> In that moment, I'd never wanted to be human more, just so I could be with Ezekiel Crosse. Zeke, who was brave and loyal and selfless, who hated vampires but was still here, surrounded by them, because of me. Who had left Eden and traveled across the country, to New Covington, because he wanted to bring me home. <br>And I could never go with him. -Allison<br><br><b>4.</b> No matter what it took and how hard I had to fight it, I would not become a monster. -Allison<br><br><b>5.</b> For the rest of my existence, if I lived to see the end of the world, there would never be another Ezekiel Crosse. There would never be another soul as bright as his. And that both terrified me and made me savagely--and maybe selfishly--determined to keep him. Zeke was mine now. Forever. -Allison<br><br><b>6.</b> I cared for him more than I'd cared for anyone in my life save my mom. It would <b>destroy</b> me if I lost him now. -Allison<br><br><b>7.</b> Loss was just a part of life, I knew that. Nothing lasted in this world. The harder you held on to something, the more it would kill you when it is gone, so it was best not to get attached to anything. -Allison<br><br><b>8</b> Dammit, what good is immortality if I can't help the ones I care about? If I have to spend eternity alone? -Allison<br><br><b>9</b> There are no good choices, Allison. There are only those you can live with, and those you can work to change. -Kanin<br><br><b>10</b> He was right about Sarren, and he was right about his very first rule of vampirism. But it was far too late now. I was attached. And if Zeke was gone, I didn't know what I would do. -Allison<br><br><b>11</b> Let me release you from this mortal coil, and send you gently into the eternal night. -Sarren<br><br>ETERNAL NIGHT. Ohgod. Is that enough foreshadowing or what. <br><br><b>12.</b> And the monster rose up, embracing my pain, turning it to vengeance. <i>This is what we are</i>, it whispered, easing the despair threatening to crush me. <i>We are vampires. We are not human, we do not need human emotion, we do not get attached to human beings. You knew that from the beginning.</i><br><br>I did. Allie the Fringer knew that, even before she was Turned. She'd tried to warn me to keep my distance, to guard my heart. <br><br>Lesson learned. I was a monster. I would never forget that again.<br><br>--<br><br><b>AFTER READING</b> <i>23 June 2013 </i>: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380375986ra/730686.gif" width="350" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That is the most horrible ending ever made in the history of forever. I don't...I can't even...How can you do this to all your fans, Julie? I thought we had something special. And then you do this. My worst nightmare.<br><br>I'm starting to think that all authors are sadists. They enjoy our pain. I bet they're now laughing at our miseries.<br><br>Author: Look at all these mundane readers...I should write slower. Make them suffer. Don't you agree, publishers?<br>Publishers: Oh, yes. Don't you just enjoy reading about their agony? So how long shall we make them wait this time? Six months? Nine months? A year? <br>Author: Based on that cliffhanger I left for them, I think a year, at least. This is going to be lovely.<br>*insert evil laughter here* <br><br>***********************************<br><br>I WOULD BE ETERNALLY GRATEFUL IF SOMEONE WOULD LIKE TO GIVE ME A COPY OF THE PAPERBACK VERSION. <br><br>I mean, look at how beautiful the cover is: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1362735567l/17455977.jpg" width="250" height="380" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>UPDATE</b> <i>19 April 2013, 11 days before publication</i>: I am still patiently waiting for the <b>
  <u>REAL</u>
</b> cover to come out.......<br><br><b>UPDATE</b> <i>15 December 2012</i>: I like the cover of The Immortal Rules, even though the cover girl is not Asian. BUT WHY WOULD THEY WANT TO CHANGE THE COVER? Ugggh. Now my books wont match! <br><br>Why couldn't they just leave that cover for the paperback version? <br><br><b>UPDATE</b> <i>20 October 2012</i>: OMG. It's coming!! <br><br>..on April 1, 2013. I'M A FANGIRL, I DO NOT DO CALM. <br><br>I hope this isn't one those annoying times when someone tells you something really great on April 1st and then they say "April fools!" If so, I'm gonna go hang myself. <br><br><b>UPDATE</b> <i>03 September 2012</i>: OMG, people!!! It now has a blurb. I think I'm shipping to Team Kanin. :&gt; <br><br><b>UPDATE</b> <i>May-August Update:</i> Oh dear gods. It has a title. <i>The Eternity Cure</i>. Sounds really... cool. <br><br><b>Original review:</b> Oh god. Another reason for me to endure my miserable existence! I'm dying to see the cover, the blurb, and read this!<br><br>...and I just know that this will be awesome. Julie Kagawa will never let us down! <br><br><b>Can't 2013 come any faster? I'm dying here!</b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_602911898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/602911898" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/602911898?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848451858" href="/book/show/17453202-the-eternity-cure">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2013">reviewed-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=so-many-vampires">so-many-vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-action">all-action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=best-of-2013">best-of-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=just-another-book-crush">just-another-book-crush</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=open-ending">open-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=role-models">role-models</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer602911898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13788458965593541703"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/>The last two books in Julie Kagawa’s impressive bibliography – first The Lost Prince and now The Eternity Cure – show a certain level of maturity and self-assuredness that simply wasn’t there before. I always enjoyed her books, even those first few ones in which she relied on familiar mythology and tropes, but now that she trusts herself enough to fly solo, <i>like</i> has become too small a word for how I feel. In The Eternity Cure more than ever before, Kagawa kept all the fine threads tight</span>
  <span id="freeText13788458965593541703" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br>The last two books in Julie Kagawa’s impressive bibliography – first The Lost Prince and now The Eternity Cure – show a certain level of maturity and self-assuredness that simply wasn’t there before. I always enjoyed her books, even those first few ones in which she relied on familiar mythology and tropes, but now that she trusts herself enough to fly solo, <i>like</i> has become too small a word for how I feel. In The Eternity Cure more than ever before, Kagawa kept all the fine threads tightly in control. <br><br>Things that bothered me in The Immortal Rules, like lack of backstory and worldbuilding, were neatly taken care of with Dawn of Eden, a prequel novella published in the <i>‘Til the World Ends</i> anthology. Going into this sequel with the <i>hows</i> and <i>whys</i> properly explained allowed me to relax and sink into the story without the constant nagging questions rising at the back of my mind.<br><br>Our long-awaited reunion with Allison Sekemoto brings with it a few surprises. Months have passed since she left Eden behind, and while she’s getting closer to Kanin every day, she still hasn’t found him. After so many months spent in solitude, searching fruitlessly for her Sire, Allie is a somewhat different vampire. She is much stronger and far more confident, but even more importantly, she knows who and <i>what</i> she is, and although she suffers from occasional bursts of nostalgia, she never whines or wallows in self-pity anymore. This Allie is someone I can get behind, a person (oh, fine, a vampire) I can admire. <br><br>It’s probably why I felt so strongly about the romance this time, when it failed to touch me at all in the first book. Back then, I simply didn’t understand the attraction between her and Zeke, it seemed like something included <i>pro forma</i> rather than a passionate, heartfelt thing. Allie is not the only one who’s changed, matured. Zeke is hardened, different, but still the kind, gentle boy somewhere underneath. Still, this new and improved version seemed somehow more believable in those circumstances. To explain it like a vampire would: he stopped being prey and became a hunter instead.<br><br>After reading dozens of reviews, I think it’s safe to conclude that Jackal, Allie’s blood brother, is the readers’ favorite. I just love redeemed characters, but I love characters that dance on that fine line between good and bad, likeable and obnoxious, even more. Allie kept having to remind herself to hate him for what he’s done, and I had the same problem, although it’s safe to say Zeke never came near forgiving and forgetting. Jackal brought with him what the first book sorely lacked – a wonderful sense of humor. Without him, this would have been an action-packed, tense, but humorless adventure.<br><br>As much as I enjoyed my love-hate relationship with Jackal, Kanin remains my favorite. Quiet and solemn, he seemed a bit more approachable this time around, and possibly a bit warmer too, especially towards Allie. We finally learned about his past, and the revelations were timed perfectly. Instead of turning me and everyone else against him, they just made me love him even more.<br><br>The Eternity Cure is positively addictive and it took me completely by surprise. As someone who felt merely lukewarm about the first book, I didn’t expect to love it as much as I did, but I said exactly the same about The Lost Prince. I won’t make the same mistake a third time.<br><br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br></span>

<div id="review_308895108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308895108" />
    <a title="Suzanne " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5952567-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411233665p2/5952567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308895108?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne " href="/user/show/5952567-suzanne">Suzanne </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848451858" href="/book/show/17453202-the-eternity-cure">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5952567-suzanne?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5952567-suzanne?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308895108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17261376147829575049">I really enjoyed The Immortal Rules, with Kanin winning a place in my heart. After what we seen happen to him then, I was anxiously awaiting the release of The Eternity Cure and looked forward to journeying with Allie to find and save him. What I didn't expect was to finish this book with a new favourite character, Jackal, who really made this book for me. <br/><br/>The book opens with Allie, alone, and following the blood tie she has to Kanin as he's her sire. She's been dreaming of him and the torture t</span>
  <span id="freeText17261376147829575049" style="display:none">I really enjoyed The Immortal Rules, with Kanin winning a place in my heart. After what we seen happen to him then, I was anxiously awaiting the release of The Eternity Cure and looked forward to journeying with Allie to find and save him. What I didn't expect was to finish this book with a new favourite character, Jackal, who really made this book for me. <br /><br />The book opens with Allie, alone, and following the blood tie she has to Kanin as he's her sire. She's been dreaming of him and the torture that he's being put through at the hands of Sarren, the psycho vamp. She won't give up until she finds him, she wouldn't be where she is now without him. He saved her life when she was attacked by rabids, and then thought her how to live as a vampire. But I found this wandering tedious and boring, making the first 100 pages or so of this book, not quite as enjoyable as I was expecting, or as the rest of the book, thankfully, turned out to be. Once Allie meets up with Jackal I was hooked. <br /><br />We first met Jackal in The Immortal Rules where he was cruel and vicious. He has an army of human followers, but he is on a mission to find a cure for the red lung disease, and then plans to turn them into a vampire army. I hated him with passion then. But in The Eternity Cure, while he is still cruel and vicious, still searching for the cure, still planning his army, and kills humans without any concious thought, we also see another side to him. He is sarcastic and witty and adds a lot of humour to this book. <br /><br />Kanin is much the same in this book as he was in The Immortal Rules and still as likable. After all he's been through over the past few months, he doesn't show signs of it having had a lasting impact on him, he's stoic and calm, and seems to hold his head quite well in dire situations. <br /><br />Foolishly, I wasn't expecting to see Zeke return in this book, he was in Eden, and I expected him to stay there. I liked Zeke even more in this book than in the first one. He's a tougher, stronger, harder Zeke. Where I kind of felt he was a little too 'good' previously, he didn't seem to have that same persona here. He's still good, and extremely caring for everyone, but tough and less of a doormat here. He's out for revenge and we see that past events have definitely taken a toll on poor Zeke. I feel more pity towards him now, funnily enough, than after he lost his father and friends at the hands of Jackal.<br /><br />A large majority of this book is spent travelling, a lot of which is through the sewers. Again, Kagawa's world building is faultless. And, I have to commend her recapping, I don't have the best memory and often find myself quite lost going into sequels, but not here. It was quite easy to pick up where I'd left off with The Immortal Rules. <br /><br />Julie left me in shock with the ending. And with no information yet on the third book, I just hope we're not going to be left hanging too long.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17261376147829575049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_349619061" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349619061" />
    <a title="Joie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6224284-joie"><img alt="Joie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453104735p2/6224284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349619061?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joie" href="/user/show/6224284-joie">Joie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349619061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12595492921707764908"><b>Actual rating: 4.5 stars </b><br/><br/>As far as sequels go, I'm glad to say that <i>The Eternity Cure</i> did not disappoint- which was quite a feat considering how much I loved <i>The Immortal Rules</i>. This book made me feel so many things- from anxiety to anticipation to short-lived joy to heartache- that I'm going to have to break down this review piece by piece.<br/><br/><b>The Characters<br/>Allie.</b> Badass as ever. She is both fierce and fearsome, which makes for a great vampire, yet she also carries vulnerabilities and insecurities,</span>
  <span id="freeText12595492921707764908" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 4.5 stars </b><br><br>As far as sequels go, I'm glad to say that <i>The Eternity Cure</i> did not disappoint- which was quite a feat considering how much I loved <i>The Immortal Rules</i>. This book made me feel so many things- from anxiety to anticipation to short-lived joy to heartache- that I'm going to have to break down this review piece by piece.<br><br><b>The Characters<br>Allie.</b> Badass as ever. She is both fierce and fearsome, which makes for a great vampire, yet she also carries vulnerabilities and insecurities, which makes for a great, relatable protagonist. In this book, Allie is really starting to come into her own, accepting and embracing her new vampire life. I'm really excited to see where Kagawa takes this character in the next book. Especially with the way this one ended.....<br><br><b>Zeke.</b> Bookish bad boys better watch out because Ezekial Cross is making the Nice Guy persona very swoon-worthy. My favorite thing about Zeke, aside from his innate <i>goodness</i> is his unwavering loyalty and faith. In that respect, I think he and Allie complement each other very well.<br><br><b>Jackal.</b> Oh, Ms. Kawaga.... what have you done? I think Jackal just became my favorite character in the series!! I loved how I was constantly guessing whether he would end up a hero or a villain. There are little moments when he proves to be a good ally (and great comic relief) but there is always this understanding that he can't be trusted. I guess I'm just a total sucker for morally ambiguous characters with snark. I also enjoyed his twisted sibling relationship with Allie- it brought some much needed humor and lightness into an otherwise dark story.<br><br><b>Kanin</b>...... is such and interesting character. After two books, I'm still not completely sure what to make of him. Kanin takes a bigger role in this book which was quite nice because I love his demeanor, especially in relation to all the other characters. For me, Kanin is definitely the most intriguing one to read about.<br><br>And, in case you were wondering, Sarren is still as twisted and sadistic as ever.<br><br><b>The Plot</b><br>As always, Kagawa's pacing was <i>perfect</i>. This book had me hooked from the very first chapter and kept me enraptured all the way up to that jaw-dropping ending. Literally, I openly gaped at the book when I got to the last page. But don't worry, no spoilers for you!<br><br>The most notable thing about this book was that there was a lot more gore than in The Immortal Rules. On one hand, this was nice because more action was happening throughout the book- and, really, who doesn't love awesome fight scenes? On the other hand, it did feel just a <i>tad</i> bit excessive. There are only so many pages I can stand of sword-slashing and vampiric dismemberment.<br><br><b>The Romance</b><br>This is pretty surprising for me to say, but I was a little unsatisfied with the romance. It's not that I didn't like the romantic development (because I totally support the Zeke/Allie ship) but the initial meeting between the two, namely Zeke explaining why he came after Allie, did not feel very natural to me. I may be in the minority here, but, following the events of book 1, it didn't seem like their relationship was at a point where it was realistic that Zeke did the things he did for her.<br><br><b>All in all:</b><br><i>The Eternity Cure</i> was a very riveting read. Kagawa has hit the character-plot-setting trifecta once again.<br><b>
  <i>Warning:</i>
</b> this book ends with one heck of cliffhanger. Unless it's 2014 and the third book is out, prepare junk food on hand to eat away the feelings.<br><br><br><br><b>
  <u>PRE-REVIEW</u>
</b><br><b>OHMAHGERD. DAT ENDING.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/475626.gif" width="300" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>AND NOW I HAVE TO WAIT OVER A YEAR FOR THE NEXT BOOK?!</b><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380380977ra/738085.gif" width="270" height="190" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1393780765" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Kira Simion" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27960680-kira-simion"><img alt="Kira Simion" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528008824p2/27960680.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1393780765?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kira Simion" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kira Simion" href="/user/show/27960680-kira-simion">Kira Simion</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27960680-kira-simion?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1393780765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6915636575554716070">Ohmygodohmygodohmygodohmygod!<br/><br/>5/5 beautifully bloody stars!<br/><br/>READ THE FIRST BOOK BEFORE THIS ONE! It'll help the feels. :D (Not sadness feels as much as <i> yes, kick some butt </i> feels! ;))<br/><br/>I avoided this book because usually the first book of the series is the best but, this one was even BETTER than the first one!<br/><br/><i> Review to come! </i><br/><br/><del> MWAHHAHAHAHA </del><br/><br/>When you've screamed at a book, you've probably gotten strange looks. When I screamed, cheered, and my eyes almost popped out of my head, all I could think was <i> </i></span>
  <span id="freeText6915636575554716070" style="display:none">Ohmygodohmygodohmygodohmygod!<br /><br />5/5 beautifully bloody stars!<br /><br />READ THE FIRST BOOK BEFORE THIS ONE! It'll help the feels. :D (Not sadness feels as much as <i> yes, kick some butt </i> feels! ;))<br /><br />I avoided this book because usually the first book of the series is the best but, this one was even BETTER than the first one!<br /><br /><i> Review to come! </i><br /><br /><del> MWAHHAHAHAHA </del><br /><br />When you've screamed at a book, you've probably gotten strange looks. When I screamed, cheered, and my eyes almost popped out of my head, all I could think was <i> please please please </i> don't end.<br /><br />Then it ended. On a cliffhanger....dbdksndndkdnndndmdmd is how I describe this emotion. *cries rainbows*<br /><br /><b> *. *. *. *. *. * </b><br /><br />Once in a blue moon, (*cough* Underneath the Neversky *cough*) you find a book that makes your heart race, your hands quiver, and your eyes glued in fixation.<br /><br />This book was that book (for me).<br /><br /><b> "How do you deal with the end of eternity?" </b><br /><br />-Badass heroine with badass companions that have their own personality that makes me love them <del> and want them to be real. </del><br /><br />-Jackal. <i> Oh </i> Jackal. How I loved how you were a (somewhat) asshole with your clever remarks. I was giggling crazily and got quite a few strange looks. <del> Oh well.<br /></del><br />-Allison. I absolutely <b> <i> loved </i></b>  your character. Your personality was real. Your problems were handled with certainly but, you weren't perfect and you showed your human side to me. <i> Thank you. </i><br /><br />-Allison's sire, Kanin, is a beautiful soul. <i> See the irony? </i> He is said to <i> have </i> no soul but, he shows it over and over, choosing humans over vampires but, only killing the "worst" vampires or the rabbids or the crazed infected humans/vampires. He is wise and shows his years of experience with his actions and words. I would like a mentor like him. I would be honored to have one like him. I <i> want </i> him as my teacher.<br /><br /><del> Please? </del><br /><br />-Ezekiel. Hello there my friend. You have gone through hard times and continue to go through tough times. <i> Especially </i> after the cliff hanger ending.<br /><br />Damn is that a cliff hanger.... <del> Curse you for being so enjoyable! </del><br /><br />-The characters were absolutely remarkable!<br /><br />I fell in love with them and I hope they continue to stay in the land of the living, both the vampires and the human. I love them and hope the last story doesn't change their personalities (too much). (I have high hopes)!<br /><br />-The plot was splendid. While there was a main plot that connected to the first book, there were many many subplots, romance (not too much that you choke), action scenes that had me excited for the next page, and twists! (Not plot twists but twists. The difference is the predictability and the curving of the story around the subplots).<br /><br />5/5 on to the next book stars!<br /><br /><b> Edit: </b><br /><br /><i> If </i> this series is made into a movie, the producers <i> BETTER </i> have an Asian main character. If anyone gets offended, I am <del> not </del> sorry. I have just waaaaay too many bad remakes where the producers don't follow the book (and change the main character's looks). (Though on occasions there are good movies based on books too). Maybe that's just what happens. I suppose movies are never as good as the book. *sigh*</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=out-2013">out-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer477758633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8885666790934987485"><i>“This is what I am, I thought, walking forward to join them. This is where I belong, in the darkness. We’re vampires. That’s all we’ll ever be”</i><br/><br/>Once again when I’ve found myself stumbling through books and in a reading slump, Kagawa is the one to pull me out of it. I had high hopes for The Eternity Cure after adoring The Immortal Rules last year but The Eternity Cure exceeded all my expectations. I have so much love for this book right now that I think my review will just be full of incoherent ba</span>
  <span id="freeText8885666790934987485" style="display:none"><i>“This is what I am, I thought, walking forward to join them. This is where I belong, in the darkness. We’re vampires. That’s all we’ll ever be”</i><br /><br />Once again when I’ve found myself stumbling through books and in a reading slump, Kagawa is the one to pull me out of it. I had high hopes for The Eternity Cure after adoring The Immortal Rules last year but The Eternity Cure exceeded all my expectations. I have so much love for this book right now that I think my review will just be full of incoherent babbling and gushing, so I’m doing my review for this book a little bit differently. <br /><br />The Characters. <br />With The Immortal Rules we were introduced to a range of characters which quite easily found a place in my heart. I thought I knew what these characters were really like then, and once again Kagawa was easy to remind me why I became so fond of them in the first place; especially of Kanin, Allie and Zeke. These three were an unlikely trio, but the way everything had been left ravaged they had come together with the same end goal. What I admired about all three was despite their clear differences, they were willing to work together, put their life on their line, for each other no question asked. Their time together was laced with humorous scenes, but also scenes which had me choking up with tears. Those who were disappointed with the amount of Kanin in The Immortal Rules will be pleased with this latest instalment. I had high hopes for his character in this book and that we would get to know his character more and I will say the wait was definitely worth it. Allie couldn’t have asked for a better sire. His resilience, determination and always attempting to do what was right despite time being against him I truly admired. These characteristics were clearly strong in Allie’s character too. Then we had our “secondary characters” I guess I can’t really call them that because of how much of a direct impact they had on this book. With these characters Kagawa was the monster of toying with your feelings; there were no clear cut answers with them, you never knew what they would do next, if you could trust them, but they triggered so many emotions within me of; confusion, laughter, hatred and rage. You know when you’re a kid and you’re watching a cartoon, and a villain is brought in to mess with the good guys like Mufasa in The Lion King, some of these characters especially with Sarren and Stick evoked all those feelings that I used to have as I had as a kid, where you’re just furious, and nothing can be the same until you’ve throttled them to death. Kagawa definitely took it up a whole another notch with these brilliant set of characters. If you thought your heart had been pushed to the limits with The Immortal Rules, just wait. <br /><br />World building. <br />The Eternity Cure did take me a while to get into, but after a few pages, this crazy world Kagawa created completely pulled me in. I was completely taken in by the chaos and destruction and every new mission that Allie had to complete. Kagawa was able to make this crazy world appear so real, that everything Allie was going through I felt I was experiencing it alongside with her. Despite New Covington being dangerous and infested, I felt myself invested in this story until the very end, until we had the answers we needed. So to sum the world building was pure brilliance! <br /><br />Surprise Factors. <br />Just like in The Immortal Rules, my heart was in my throat the entire time with The Eternity Cure. I was on high alert all the time, never letting my guard down, as you never knew what was lurking around the corner. With The Eternity Cure you just have to be prepared for the unexpected; there’s endless surprises which will cause heartache; as if you have a knife slicing through your heart, and just will have you reeling with aftershocks. And then there are others which will cause you great amount of rage. I think these were the two strongest emotions that this book evoked within me; heartache and rage. My poor heart and blood pressure barely survived with every single blow. <br /><br />The Ending. <br />I have no words...how could you do this to me Ms. Kagawa? <br /><br />This year I have been struggling to find books which have completely blown me away, thus the reason why The Eternity Cure is only my second 5 star rated book of the year so far. But honestly if I could give this book 100 stars I would as it was that damn good. Bring on 2014, for the next instalment, I’m pretty sure by that time my heart will have been taped back together and I will be raring to go for whatever Kagawa has to offer. *cowers in corner and cries to self* </span>
  <a data-text-id="8885666790934987485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_308841570" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308841570" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308841570?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781743562604" href="/book/show/17455977-the-eternity-cure">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=bite-me">bite-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308841570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3863384600605250160">It's no secret that one of my all time favorite authors is Julie Kagawa and there is a reason why. She doesn't know how to write a bad book. In fact, I'm pretty sure she just gets better and better with every new release.<br/><br/><b>The Eternity Cure</b> is the much anticipated sequel to Julie's vampire series, <i>Blood of Eden</i>. <br/>We begin our story with Allison searching for her sire, Kanin. Blood calls to blood and Allie has seen the bloodcurdling nightmares of her sire's imprisonment and endless torture at the ha</span>
  <span id="freeText3863384600605250160" style="display:none">It's no secret that one of my all time favorite authors is Julie Kagawa and there is a reason why. She doesn't know how to write a bad book. In fact, I'm pretty sure she just gets better and better with every new release.<br /><br /><b>The Eternity Cure</b> is the much anticipated sequel to Julie's vampire series, <i>Blood of Eden</i>. <br />We begin our story with Allison searching for her sire, Kanin. Blood calls to blood and Allie has seen the bloodcurdling nightmares of her sire's imprisonment and endless torture at the hands of the monstrous Sarren. She will do everything in her power to find him and save him from his living hell. But on her journey to search for her master, she finds an old enemy who turns out to be an unlikely ally. They discover that a new strain of Red Lung Virus has been unleashed, giving humans and even vampires horrific effects. <br />They need to find a cure and time is running out...for everyone.<br /><br />Wow! What a sequel! I've always adored Julie's writing, she has such an incredible way with words and she is just such a fierce storyteller. When I think back to all my other vampire series, I have to say that this one has to be the most disturbing of the bunch. Julie's world is thick and heavy cloaked in darkness, madness and desperation. It's raw agony punches us into emotional turmoil and just when we're on a the edge of hope looking up, we're thrown over that same edge, tumbling down. This is everything a vampire book should be and more. You wont find fluff-n-stuff here my friends. This world is dire, dangerous and deathly. I admit, I do miss the lighter moments and even the humor Julie is gifted for, but I have to say that I'm loving how different this experience is compared to other vampire reads. This is the kind of world where I'm afraid to breath. It's not overly graphic but it's graphic enough to power our imagination into overdrive, making us terrified and heartbroken in the same breath. It's very hard to get through some of those more painful scenes, especially if your already very much attached to these characters.<br /><br />There is a lot that happens plot wise. So many twist and turns on the road to finding a cure and stopping an insatiable psychopathic monster who's only appetite is total and complete utter destruction.<br />Allie has grown up since the first book. Being a vampire has hardened her in ways she can't control, but she still fights her inner-demons and clings to the notion that she can still choose what kind of monster she wants to be. She's still such a force. Confident, strong, passionate, determined and loyal.<br />Her unlikely alley turns out to be someone that I would have never expected. Jackal has wormed his way into my good graces and affections. Only Kagawa can accomplish redemption in a character I would have loved to see staked after what he did to Zeke's family, only I find myself believing in him instead.<br />Kaine has been through the worse kind of hell. He still wears his regret like a scar and still remains wise and controlled as ever. But the way he wants to set things right and the way he holds himself up with such a distinguished manner and vulnerability, makes me want to follow him till the very end.<br />Fans will be happy to see that Zeke is very much in this installment. He and Allie have some of the most sweetest moments that makes this journey worth fighting for. But the road to happiness is not paved smooth (it never is in Kagawa's world) so be warned that dark heartbreaking times are still up ahead.<br />And lastly we have Sarren. Possibly the worst villain I've ever read. I want a slow painful death for this character. His thriving blood-lust for revenge is sick and demented. He is pure evil and I'll be on the edge of my seat cheering on to see the way Kagawa ends him. And she <i>must</i> end him.<br /><br />Bottom line, The Eternity Cure is another unflinching, unforgiving and unmerciful installment in the Blood of Eden series. Julie Kagawa has out done herself. She has proven time and time again that she can write just about anything and even has me anticipating freezer-worthy horror, and if you know me, that's saying something. Fans of The Immortal Rules will want to get their hands on this spine-tingling sequel as soon as possible. I can't wait to see where Kagawa takes us and these characters next. I'm scared and anxious, specially after that evil-cliffy of an ending! MORE!<br /><br />(Arc provided by Netgalley and Harlequin Teen AU)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3863384600605250160" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qpC433diNpbG159LzrtFf2v7kQFnVj1FqijNnAgrrC+QttENzDz//mH8Kyo5Tk+gvaR2yanbsyLxVostxWhetQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UfpCfbV21EEASK0niTX0xqHxCrXzfhM9Unlrh0s1yHFr3CuvDigdKadjGUZ+wP4Zd67tfT3znVoJBy02hnY66w==')})
  }
//]]>
